  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8af9f884-44c0-442e-b527-8bc8e4a667b2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText15659707793480185430" style="display:none"><b>One single mom. One chaotic family. One quirky stranger. One irresistible love story from the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>The Giver of Stars</i><br /></b><br />  <br /> American audiences have fallen in love with Jojo Moyes. Ever since she debuted Stateside she has captivated readers and reviewers alike, and hit the <i>New York Times</i> bestseller list with the word-of-mouth sensation <i>Me Before You</i>. Now, with <i>One Plus One</i>, she’s written another contemporary opposites-attract love story.<br />  <br /> Suppose your life sucks. A lot. Your husband has done a vanishing act, your teenage stepson is being bullied, and your math whiz daughter has a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity that you can’t afford to pay for. That’s Jess’s life in a nutshell—until an unexpected knight in shining armor offers to rescue them. Only Jess’s knight turns out to be Geeky Ed, the obnoxious tech millionaire whose vacation home she happens to clean. But Ed has big problems of his own, and driving the dysfunctional family to the Math Olympiad feels like his first unselfish act in ages . . . maybe ever.<br />  <br /><i>One Plus One</i> is Jojo Moyes at her astounding best. You’ll laugh, you’ll weep, and when you flip the last page, you’ll want to start all over again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15659707793480185430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/395909-did-anyone-else-notice-this-incongruity-in">Did anyone else notice this incongruity in the story? When Ed goes to buy glasses for Tanzie, he describes taking Norman with him, but when Nicky describes what took place at the Maths Olympiad while Ed was gone, he describes having Norman with them. The dog seems to be two places at once...</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_395909'><a id="like_count_community_question_395909" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/395909?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F23359964-one-plus-one">like</a></span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4057814-loretta"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1490744097i/4057814._UY100_CR26,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4057814-loretta">Loretta</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You are absolutely right. <br/>Page 204: Ed drops them off and says "you guys go in and register, I'll get her some glasses." It then describes Norman bein<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You are absolutely right. <br />Page 204: Ed drops them off and says "you guys go in and register, I'll get her some glasses." It then describes Norman being in the car with him while he looks for the shop.<br />Page 215: Jess is at the desk registering Tanzie, Nicky is off to the side WITH Norman to keep him out of everyone's way when he notices the two boys pestering Tanzie. He then ties Norman's lead to a radiator to go deal with them. The next page they are talking about how they are still waiting for Ed to get back with some glasses.<br />So, yes...Norman is in two places at once.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_679361844" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679361844" />
    <a title="Jan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2845570-jan"><img alt="Jan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530803515p2/2845570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679361844?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan" href="/user/show/2845570-jan">Jan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781405915571" href="/book/show/18186807-the-one-plus-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2845570-jan?shelf=my-top-20-2013">my-top-20-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679361844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2029785956733180939">I read this a while ago and now reviews are starting to pop up everywhere I thought I'd add mine.<br/><br/>I feel I should begin this review with an apology to Diane Chamberlain ... Whenever I'm asked who my favourite author is - I name her, as she never fails to delight and presses all my buttons with her lovely romantic family dramas - Well I'm sorry Diane, I'm not dumping you, honest I'm not, its just that Jojo Moyes is my flavour of the month at the moment and looks to be taking top spot for some time</span>
  <span id="freeText2029785956733180939" style="display:none">I read this a while ago and now reviews are starting to pop up everywhere I thought I'd add mine.<br /><br />I feel I should begin this review with an apology to Diane Chamberlain ... Whenever I'm asked who my favourite author is - I name her, as she never fails to delight and presses all my buttons with her lovely romantic family dramas - Well I'm sorry Diane, I'm not dumping you, honest I'm not, its just that Jojo Moyes is my flavour of the month at the moment and looks to be taking top spot for some time yet, I feel almost as though I'm being unfaithful but she just gets better and BETTER.<br /><br />When I was offered an advance galley of the new book by Jojo Moyes to read and review through the wonderful Netgalley - I was delighted, I adored "the girl you left behind" and so loved her book "Me before you", I really didn't think she could even come close to writing anything that good ever again.<br /><br />Well I was wrong! She HAS done it again and completely blown me away with her latest romantic novel "the one plus one". I just knew from the first few pages it was going to be something special - you know when you pick up a new book and with some you think "OK I'm sure I'll get into this soon", or "Hmm this looks good", and on the all too rare occasion you get a shiver down your back and go ... "OMG this is AMAZING" - straight off, well that's what I did with this - shivers - immediately.<br /><br />It's a simple storyline, really. At the start we are introduced to Jess, single parent of a young daughter and stepson, working as a cleaner, living on a sink estate, scrimping and struggling to make ends meet - and this is done so beautifully I found it impossible to believe Jess wasn't someone not only real but very well known to me, I kept wanting to shout out loud at things she thought and felt "me TOO" <br /><br />Jess really wants better for her kids, and they are amazing kids - down to earth, real, loveable and flawed. Daughter Tanzie 8 years old going on 80, doesn't fit in at school, is regarded as a swot for her passion and uncanny ability with maths. Her stepbrother Nicky, full of teenage angst, Goth verging on Hippy, picked on for his differentness, finds it hard to relate to anyone.<br /><br />When Tanzie is offered the opportunity of a lifeline, Jess tries desperately to seize the chance for her to gain a scholarship to the school of her dreams but being a real person, and therefore not perfect, Jess makes a few bad decisions and what follows is a comic tragedy of grand proportions - resulting in a journey of a lifetime and the opportunity to change all their lives - but can she make the most of it or will she just make everything a whole lot worse?<br /><br />Enter Ed, with a story of his own to tell - his life's falling apart and the very last thing he needs in his life are a cleaner, her 2 weird kids and their flatulent, farting, hearth rug of a dog, but he gets sucked into their story and as his own situation gets worse he tries to help Jess - and the unlikely couple hit it off against all odds, even though they are from lifestyles too diverse to even be able to relate to one anothers' problems.<br /><br />The emotions this book stirs up are very mixed - I gasped aloud with laughter many times, (and it takes quite a lot to tickle my funny bone) I shrieked aloud and I sobbed. My vocabulary can't even begin to do justice to just quite how brilliant I think this book is, how much I loved it. <br /><br />The sheer poetry of Jojo Moyes writing elevates this page turner of a romance, way above the genre of chick-lit and into the realms of literary fiction, such a pleasure to read and an easy to follow story told with amazing assurance and realism. Every word a joy to read from start to finish. I loved all the main characters especially Norman the great lump of canine daftness and unswerving loyalty who is their dog.<br /><br />This book is sheer class, pure quality and its what reading is all about. I'm so envious of everyone who hasn't read it yet as you've got all this pleasure ahead of you - read it and enjoy every nuance.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2029785956733180939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2356984860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2356984860" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2356984860?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525426585" href="/book/show/18693716-one-plus-one">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2356984860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3381711371560076901"><b>2.7</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote> “You know, you spend your whole life feeling like you don’t quite fit in anywhere. And then you walk into a room one day, whether it’s at university or an office or some kind of club, and you just go, ‘Ah. There they are.’ And suddenly you feel at home.” <br/><br/>― Jojo Moyes, One Plus One </blockquote><br/><br/>This was a good book. With good characters. A good storyline. And a good romance. But it only got this far. To the adjective "good". This was one of the easy-to-read books you read when you're bore</span>
  <span id="freeText3381711371560076901" style="display:none"><b>2.7</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote> “You know, you spend your whole life feeling like you don’t quite fit in anywhere. And then you walk into a room one day, whether it’s at university or an office or some kind of club, and you just go, ‘Ah. There they are.’ And suddenly you feel at home.” <br /><br />― Jojo Moyes, One Plus One </blockquote><br /><br />This was a good book. With good characters. A good storyline. And a good romance. But it only got this far. To the adjective "good". This was one of the easy-to-read books you read when you're bored, when you literally have nothing to do with your life at the moment and just pick this random book up you know is gonna be convenient to read. A book you don't care much about what happens to the characters, a book you won't remember in some time, but also a book you can't leave down just because the plot in chick lits many times gets intense.<br /><br />We have our main character, Jess. She has two jobs, two kids, a dog, huge ass financial problems and a huge ass prick of an ex. We have Tanzie, Jess' gifted daughter, more than talented with math who can't find her moment to shine, we got Nicky, Jess' ex' kid who she got under her custody, that is bullied in school, and Norman, their fucking huge ass lazy dog, who is a brave warrior inside. Then we got Ed, a rich developer who's about to be convicted for fraud, there at the right time to help the family... the knight in shinning armor. <br /><br />I had many problems with Jess as a character. She was going through so many turmoils in her life, mostly financially, and I understood. I really understood. But she was so disrespectful to Ed, especially in the beginning. The man offered, with no reciprocation whatsoever, a total stranger to them, to get them in time in Scotland on Tanzie's behalf, a three day journey, and there we have Jess throwing her legs up on the dash of his expensive AUDI, being rude to him, causing trouble with food because "she couldn't go to McDonald's", and basically being a bitch all the time. And the other thing... oh man that thing. The thing where she thought she was superior to everyone because she was poor. She treated Ed like his money grew on a fucking tree. Like he didn't work hard to obtain them, like he didn't deserve his wealth. I was pissed off. Life is like that, you know. Some people have money some people don't. Some people work hard for them, some people don't. Some people work hard and never get wealthy some people don't. It's how the world is. Don't be an asshole about it. Being poor doesn't make you an innocent butterfly. And not all rich people are rude and condescending. I'm a poor person too, so I don't have any privilege but I wanted Jess to be more respectful towards a man who offered her and her family everything.<br /><br />Furthermore, the romance. After all the weird looks and talks, the awkward silences and the bad situations, we have a romance blooming. I liked the romance, the characters fit well together but it was too rushed and overdramatic, in my opinion. And I think this deep connection they felt with each other happened right after they had sex. Instantly. And all this dramatic bullshit "I can't live without him." "She has left a hole in my life that can't be filled and I can't stop thinking about her." was too motherfucking rushed. You realize they spent four days together, right? They might have gone through a motherload of shit but it was still four days. A person can't leave a hole inside your soul after four days, come on. No matter how good the sex was. <br /><br />Apart from that, the way the plots ended were too unrealistic. I was rolling my eyes so hard at how everything was fixing itself. Severe situations that were too dramatic by themselves miraculously being solved just with pure coincidences. It got out of hand, after a certain point. Life is not like that. I hope it was. <br /><br />Aside from all the bad things, this book had good elements. I liked the multi POV way Moyes writes, I enjoyed it in her other two books I read too, the pacing was good, at some parts it lacked speed but it didn't get me bored and the characters didn't feel flat to me. I ain't gonna lie, I enjoyed reading this book and its little unrealistic twists but it was too problematic for me to give it a good rating. Moyes always succeeds in making books that are hard to leave down. I don't know if I'll ever read something more of hers, but she has intrigued me as an author.<br /><br />Overall, a book with an interesting premise and a good set of character, humor and romance but with too many problems, in my opinion. If you want a quick and easy read, this is the book for ya. And till the next one... K BYE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3381711371560076901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1567205547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567205547" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1567205547?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20066447-the-one-plus-one">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/28953843-jennifer-masterson">Jennifer Masterson</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=definitely-not-young-adult">definitely-not-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567205547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4272882420520912583"><br/>I am not a stranger to what it means to live by making ends meet, to just have enough before the next payday comes and sometimes, just sometimes, I feel bad that I couldn’t get the ones I love more than what they need. But to a single mom like Jessica or Jess, to be rich simply means to be able to stay at home, read books and just be with your family without having to worry about the money all the bloody time which kind of made me feel like a douche because the story made me realize that I AM ri</span>
  <span id="freeText4272882420520912583" style="display:none"><br />I am not a stranger to what it means to live by making ends meet, to just have enough before the next payday comes and sometimes, just sometimes, I feel bad that I couldn’t get the ones I love more than what they need. But to a single mom like Jessica or Jess, to be rich simply means to be able to stay at home, read books and just be with your family without having to worry about the money all the bloody time which kind of made me feel like a douche because the story made me realize that I AM rich. I was just too full of myself to see it and for a book to make me turn over a new leaf, IT IS something. This book is definitely something. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes" title="Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Jojo Moyes</a> is best known for her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a> but I must say, she deserves more praises for this novel. This was so unexpected, not your typical chick-lit. It’s profound, deeply relevant and undeniably true. The would-have-been simple plot, to get Tanzie (Jess’ little girl, a Math prodigy) to the Math Olympiad has turned into something adventurous (there’s an awesome, hilarious road trip, yay!) when the family [composed of Jess, Tanzie, Nick (Jess’ stepson) and a huge lazy, slobbery dog] had to require the help of a stranger (Ed,who at first I hated but who I eventually learned to appreciate). <b>The sum of them added up to something better.</b> Please see super cute cover for illustration. <b>*fangirls over the cover*</b><br /><br />The characters were done really well and the narrative style (in the third person omniscient) is very impressive. It’s every character’s perspective without actually having to read a particular character whine about his woes or brag about his accomplishments. Things were presented truthfully without sugarcoating stuff that are sad but without being mean at the same time. Gah! I just love the author’s writing style! <b>It’s charming, funny, painful, sad but really hopeful too and worry not because nobody dies. Whoopee! </b><br /><br /><b>Happy Early Birthday, Dear <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/959167425?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">(Ate) Jennifer! (March 4 is her actual birthday)</a>. I found this perfect birthday message for you. Stay the way you are and time will never put its mark on your beautiful soul! Happy Birthday! &lt;3 </b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4272882420520912583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1011210163" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011210163" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011210163?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781611762730" href="/book/show/18693839-one-plus-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011210163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer103653034966568916"><b>One Plus One</b> was just soooo good! It was a well rounded story with romance, quirky humor, heartache, and sadness all rolled into one gorgeous story!<br/><br/>Jess Thomas has been struggling the last two years since her husband, Marty suffered a bought of depression and moved back with his mother. Financially she barely makes ends meet, even working two jobs. Add to that, her teenage son, Nicky is bullied constantly for being different (apparently goth) by schoolmates. They’ve gone to the authorities and s</span>
  <span id="freeText103653034966568916" style="display:none"><b>One Plus One</b> was just soooo good! It was a well rounded story with romance, quirky humor, heartache, and sadness all rolled into one gorgeous story!<br /><br />Jess Thomas has been struggling the last two years since her husband, Marty suffered a bought of depression and moved back with his mother. Financially she barely makes ends meet, even working two jobs. Add to that, her teenage son, Nicky is bullied constantly for being different (apparently goth) by schoolmates. They’ve gone to the authorities and school and no one will do anything. Her daughter, Tanzie is ten years old and a math genius, but she’s socially awkward. This hasn’t been a problem thus far, but when she switches up to middle school, Jess knows it’s just a matter of time before Tanzie becomes a target as well. Getting a generous scholarship to the prestigious private school, St. Anne’s, where Tanzie would thrive, seems like a prayer answered until Jess hears the cost of her share. It seems impossible until Jess hears of a Math Olympiad with its winning payout and she hatches a plan!<br /><br />Ed Nicholls has his own problems after a stupid mistake lands him in hot water and accused of insider trading. His company and the millions he’s made are in jeopardy and to top things off his father is gravely ill. Hiding out in his seaside vacation home and wallowing in self-pity is about the only things on his agenda until his path collides with Jess, Tanzie, and Nicky. The plans of getting to Scotland for Tanzie’s Math Olympiad are all but in ruins until Ed impulsively offers to drive them. Let the crazy road-trip begin! <br /><br />One Plus One is told from four different perspectives: Jess, Ed, Nicky and Tanzie. You might think this would be confusing and a little much, but it worked perfectly. Each voice added depth and richness to the story. It took a little while to get through the back story because there’s a lot going on, but once these four come together things really take off. Their trip is full of mishaps and humor, from Norman the dog and his bodily functions to buying a kabob from a dodgy food vendor that does not end well, at all! Seriously hilarious! <br /><br />I adored Jess! She was just so optimistic even with every bad thing thrown at her. She didn’t wallow in self-pity rather she looked for the good and for a workable solution. Only when Jess discovers the truth about her estranged husband does she unravel for a bit, but Ed was there to help prop her up. I was so outraged and sad for Jess! Not only was Ed there for Jess but he helped with the kids, too. Small things he did made a huge impact, especially for Nicky. But this wasn’t a story of some rich man coming along and fixing everything. Bad things still happened, and Jess dealt with them. She helped Ed, too with his perspective on life and with his family. They both helped each other:<br /><b><br />It wasn’t that Ed would make it okay—he had his own problems to deal with—but somehow the sum of them added up to something better. They would make it okay.</b><br /><br />While the romance was not the whole focus of this story, it was my favorite part. Realistic and surprisingly passionate it gave me all sorts of feels! <br /><b><br />They drove and she recalled the previous two nights in hot, dreamy fragments, his hands, his mouth,—and it was all she could do not to reach across and bury her face in his neck, to slide her hands up the back of his T-shirt for the sheer pleasure of it.</b><br /><br />As for the narration, it was superb! I highly recommend it. There were four narrators, one for each character, which is a rarity with audio books but it greatly enhanced the story. All had English accents (love!) and sounded age appropriate for the character.<br /><b><br />One Plus One</b> is just too big and wonderful to encapsulate in a review. I laughed, cried and swooned in equal measures. It was amazing on so many levels! <br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2014/08/review-one-plus-one-by-jojo-moyes.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="103653034966568916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944289249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1122592165573053614"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18693716.One_Plus_One' title='One Plus One by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>One Plus One</a> is another wonderful standalone novel written by the amazing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes' title='Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jojo Moyes</a>. I adored the characters in this novel...even the K-9 one; they all had their quirks but it works for this particular family. The events that take place in this story are funny, inspiring, as well as heartbreaking, and the message of perseverance is repeated over and over. I found myself quickly engaged in the storyline and invested in every character. I don't want to spoil anything about the story itself, so I'</span>
  <span id="freeText1122592165573053614" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18693716.One_Plus_One" title="One Plus One by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">One Plus One</a> is another wonderful standalone novel written by the amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes" title="Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Jojo Moyes</a>. I adored the characters in this novel...even the K-9 one; they all had their quirks but it works for this particular family. The events that take place in this story are funny, inspiring, as well as heartbreaking, and the message of perseverance is repeated over and over. I found myself quickly engaged in the storyline and invested in every character. I don't want to spoil anything about the story itself, so I'll sum up my review with one of the many things I took from this book:<br /><br />Is there bad in the world?<br />Yes.<br />Does the good in the world outweigh the bad?<br />Yes, Yes, Yes!<br />Thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes" title="Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Ms. Moyes</a> for the reminder. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes" title="Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Ms. Moyes</a> gently restores our faith in humanity through the eyes of multiple perspectives. The characters remind us that optimism is the only thing that keeps us going sometimes, even though that light can so easily diminish in us all. If you believe that triumph over circumstances is possible, then read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18693716.One_Plus_One" title="One Plus One by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">One Plus One</a>. I'm so glad I did!<br /><br /><b>My favorite quote:</b><br /><i>“The law of probability combined with the law of large numbers states that to beat the odds, sometimes you have to repeat an event an increasing number of times in order to get you to the outcome you desire. The more you do, the closer you get. Or, as I explain it to Mum, basically, sometimes you just have to keep going.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1122592165573053614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525426585" href="/book/show/18693716-one-plus-one">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer913258295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1059239754382969063">One Plus One was pure Hallmark--or was it Disney?--with several fucks thrown in to try to pretend it was hip instead of drip. One Plus One equals 2 boring.<br/><br/>When I was reading this, I wanted to smoke a cigarette and drink, neither of which I do. The book is just so mundane, someone needs to rebel, spice things up, and it might as well be me. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong. This book is fine. The plot is fine. The dialog is fine. Everything is fine. But fine only goes so far. Can something be too heartwarming?</span>
  <span id="freeText1059239754382969063" style="display:none">One Plus One was pure Hallmark--or was it Disney?--with several fucks thrown in to try to pretend it was hip instead of drip. One Plus One equals 2 boring.<br /><br />When I was reading this, I wanted to smoke a cigarette and drink, neither of which I do. The book is just so mundane, someone needs to rebel, spice things up, and it might as well be me. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong. This book is fine. The plot is fine. The dialog is fine. Everything is fine. But fine only goes so far. Can something be too heartwarming?<br /><br />At one point, the 8-year-old kid I babysit for was reading over my shoulder. She read the pages as fast as I did and understood the content perfectly. (Luckily, I wasn’t on one of the few pages full of “fucks”; I would have slammed the book shut, pronto!) Even she seemed bored. But really? There was something unnerving about being able to share my book with a little kid. <br /><br />I loved Me Before You and was hot to read One Plus One. The first thing I noticed, and which disappointed me, was that the basic plots of the two books were similar: earnest, spunky, nice-looking young woman who can barely make ends meet is employed by a handsome rich man--you can figure out the rest. <br /><br />There are a lot of differences between the two books though. Jess, the main character of One Plus One, has a couple of kids—one a Goth, the other a nerd. And a lot of the story takes place in a car (where there are farts and there is puke—how Disney and disgusting and sophomoric can you get?). Also, Jess is really harried, unlike the heroine in Me Before You. But talk about formulaic--surely Moyes could have come up with a different character structure for the two books. And whereas Me Before You dealt with a couple of heavy topics--the life of a quadriplegic and the issue of suicide--there was no such hook in One Plus One. The story just wasn't compelling. <br /><br />I got tired of how, throughout the whole book, we see Jess penny pinching and acting all prideful when the rich guy tries to help. Yes, it's a real bitch to be poor, and I'm not trying to be callous here. (I've sometimes had to seriously pinch pennies myself.) But Jess's tough life and obsession with her poverty, though very real and sad, was way over done. We get it. Yeah, we still get it. Move on with the story, change the channel for a while, whatever. Really, we get the picture. <br /><br />Okay, at one point she does change her tune, but it seems way too abrupt. One minute (many many minutes, actually) she is refusing to stay in a hotel that the guy insists on paying for, and the next thing you know, she is sharing a room with him. We didn't get to hear her thoughts on why she suddenly changed her mind. <br /><br />Maybe it's just that lately I've read a few heavy hitters with deeper plots and sophisticated language, because this one sure seemed too simplistic and predictable. I would have preferred that the 8-year-old I babysit for walk away because the story was beyond her comprehension. <br /><br />Despite my long list of complaints, the story was well written and I was mildly interested in what was going to happen. I didn't, however, lick my lips in gleeful anticipation when I returned to the story each day. The simplistic language and boring story got to me. I mostly wanted it to be over so I could get on to something juicier. <br /><br />Readable? Yes. Compelling? No. Would I recommend it? Not really. I did believe the characters’ emotions, and I was rooting for them, so I guess that’s something. But truth be told, it was mundane. Pass me a cigarette and a glass of wine if you would. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1059239754382969063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10616603958972342112"><b>
  <i> "A little of what you fancy does you good"</i>
</b> and this is exactly what I felt while reading One Plus One by JoJo Moyes.<br/><br/>The story is is basically an unconventional romance story and I don't normally do romance or chick lit novels but I think JoJo Moyes manages to bring a series edge to to her plots and her books are far more thought provoking than most romance novels. Having read and really enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You' title='Me Before You by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You' title='Me Before You by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1357108762s/15507958.jpg' alt='Me Before You by Jojo Moyes' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>I thought it was time for another novel by JoJo and I choose One Plus One in aud</span>
  <span id="freeText10616603958972342112" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> "A little of what you fancy does you good"</i>
</b> and this is exactly what I felt while reading One Plus One by JoJo Moyes.<br><br>The story is is basically an unconventional romance story and I don't normally do romance or chick lit novels but I think JoJo Moyes manages to bring a series edge to to her plots and her books are far more thought provoking than most romance novels. Having read and really enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1357108762s/15507958.jpg" alt="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I thought it was time for another novel by JoJo and I choose One Plus One in audio format as a running companion and I have to say it kept me engaged and interested.<br><br>I think what works in this novel is the fact that the author takes every day situations and people and weaves a story around them. I love the element of familiarity about Moye's novels as I always feel I know the characters or have met them somewhere in life. There is a lovely feel to her writing that is relaxed and airy and yet wonderful elements of emotion and humor.<br><br>A light, enjoyable read that I would recommend for the holidays.<br><br><br><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1030057025901681155"><b>BUMP FOR RELEASE DAY 7/1</b><br/><br/>Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>First – <i>massive</i> props to the good people over at NetGalley for giving me this ARC. Things could have reached an uncomfortable level of multi-requesting had you turned me down, but you didn’t so . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/xiQ43kd' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>Now, let’s get on with the show. <br/><br/>Jess’ life is not easy. She’s raising not only her 10-year old daughter Tanzie, but also her teenage stepson Nicky. Her husband split two years ago and hasn’t sent a dime to help</span>
  <span id="freeText1030057025901681155" style="display:none"><b>BUMP FOR RELEASE DAY 7/1</b><br><br>Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>First – <i>massive</i> props to the good people over at NetGalley for giving me this ARC. Things could have reached an uncomfortable level of multi-requesting had you turned me down, but you didn’t so . . . <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/xiQ43kd" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400858159ra/9728805.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Now, let’s get on with the show. <br><br>Jess’ life is not easy. She’s raising not only her 10-year old daughter Tanzie, but also her teenage stepson Nicky. Her husband split two years ago and hasn’t sent a dime to help support the kids. Now Jess works two jobs and still barely makes ends meet. Somehow through all of this she has managed to remain a “glass half full” kind of gal. <br><br>Ed’s life <i>was</i> fairly easy – until he let his judgment get clouded by an old college acquaintance who made him feel wanted again after his wife left him. Once Ed figured out he was shagging a real Stage 5 Clinger, he offered her a little bit of financial advice to get her out of his hair – only to find out that is what the pros call insider trading. Now he’s facing exorbitant fines and potential jail time – and he’s anything but optimistic.<br><br>A series of unfortunate meet-cutes has Jess and Ed at the same place at the same time – and when Jess’ car breaks down on the way to Tanzie’s Math Olympiad, Ed is the only person who can save the day – making for a road trip unlike any other.<br><br>After reading a couple of heavy books (<i>The Goldfinch</i> and <i>We Are All Completely Beside Ourselves</i>), I wanted something light. I was thrilled to see that I had been approved for this ARC, but I was also more than a little leery about starting being that I have a love (<i>Me Before You</i>) hate (<i>The Girl You Left Behind</i>) relationship with JoJo Moyes. However, I’m no coward, so I pulled up my big girl panties and dove in. <br><br>Now, this is obviously <i>not</i> Pulitizer material we’re talking about here. It’s most definitely “chick lit,” but I judge a book for the genre in which it is written and for a romance, it was everything that I wanted it to be. <br><br>I wanted humor:<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What is this?” He stared at it suspiciously.<br><br>“Scotch, triple sec, and orange juice.”<br><br>He took a sip. And then a larger one. “This is all right.”<br><br>“I knew you’d like it. I made it especially for you. It’s called a Mithering Bastard.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>and likeable characters:<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Where the hell are we, anyway?"<br><br>“Oh, somewhere on the Yellow Brick Road.”<br><br>“Is that the one with the godlike lion that saves everyone?”<br><br>“You’re thinking of Narnia. This one is cowardly and useless.”<br><br>“Figures.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>and romance:<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>He dropped his head and kissed her. He kissed her and it was a kiss of utter certainty, the kind of kiss during which monarchs die and whole continents fall without your even noticing. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I wanted to feel like the girliest girl girling out over what should be a cliché <s>boy meets girl/boy loses girl/boy gets girl back</s> girl meets boy/girl loses boy/girl gets boy back story, but what somehow instead ends up being just the right thing at the right time – and I did (and you probably will too). <br><br>This book officially comes out on July 1st. Summertime. Take a break from the serious, put on your sunscreen, take this little gem poolside and fall in love. In a couple of years I wouldn’t be surprised to see the story played out on the big screen, making “date night” a chance to fall in love all over again – like we’ve done so many times before . . .<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/hGR6LMH" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400858159ra/9728806.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/mtuWcbk" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400858159ra/9728807.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/0ZsIGbd" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400858159ra/9728808.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1836364239" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Norah Una Sumner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28782884-norah-una-sumner"><img alt="Norah Una Sumner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569421053p2/28782884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norah Una Sumner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norah Una Sumner" href="/user/show/28782884-norah-una-sumner">Norah Una Sumner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20066447-the-one-plus-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=family-theme">family-theme</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=humor">humor</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836364239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer615436580051612428"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You know, you spend your whole life feeling like you don’t quite fit in anywhere. And then you walk into a room one day, whether it’s at university or an office or some kind of club, and you just go, ‘Ah. There they are.’ And suddenly you feel at home.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Aw, I really enjoyed reading this book! I don't know what exactly did I expect but it kind of surprised me - the characters were very interesting and the whole story was quite perky at times but still serious. The storyline is not tha</span>
  <span id="freeText615436580051612428" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You know, you spend your whole life feeling like you don’t quite fit in anywhere. And then you walk into a room one day, whether it’s at university or an office or some kind of club, and you just go, ‘Ah. There they are.’ And suddenly you feel at home.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Aw, I really enjoyed reading this book! I don't know what exactly did I expect but it kind of surprised me - the characters were very interesting and the whole story was quite perky at times but still serious. The storyline is not that complicated or over-the-top dramatic which made this book much more pleasant to read, to be honest. I absolutely loved Nicky! But every character was really well-developed and showed his flaws in the best light. JoJo Moyes's writing style is great, I need to read more of her books! </span>
  <a data-text-id="615436580051612428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1574170011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1574170011" />
    <a title="Rachel Maniacup" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37103769-rachel-maniacup"><img alt="Rachel Maniacup" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516663451p2/37103769.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Maniacup" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Maniacup" href="/user/show/37103769-rachel-maniacup">Rachel Maniacup</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rachel by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=love-love">love-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=inspiring">inspiring</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1574170011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13705050471861823230">This novel for me is like,reading the <b>Attachments</b> all over again because it did give me the same,exact reaction after reading this.Yeah,you'd think it was slow and boring but I guess real good novels starts like this in the first few chapters..don't you think so?<br/><br/>So anyway,this is a story of an unusual,bizarre family where in Jessica"JESS"Rae Thomas,an amazing woman and a single parent and also the head of the family,because her husband left her two years ago leaving their two children to her(one</span>
  <span id="freeText13705050471861823230" style="display:none">This novel for me is like,reading the <b>Attachments</b> all over again because it did give me the same,exact reaction after reading this.Yeah,you'd think it was slow and boring but I guess real good novels starts like this in the first few chapters..don't you think so?<br /><br />So anyway,this is a story of an unusual,bizarre family where in Jessica"JESS"Rae Thomas,an amazing woman and a single parent and also the head of the family,because her husband left her two years ago leaving their two children to her(one isn't hers,but a son he's got from another woman,what an<br /> *---hole*),finds herself in a constant struggle to support her family by working hard.She works as a cleaner in rich peoples' houses by day,and a barmaid in a pub by night just to make ends meet.<br /><br />Added to her pains and griefs is her step-son Nicky,(the gothboy)who is oftenly bullied by some psychopatic brats who gives him a lot of bruises after beating him. Then one day,Jess received a call from her daughter,Tanzie's school,where she was offered a scholarship in one of the most admired schools in their country,exclusive to math geniuses. <br /><br />Now,in order for her to make it to that school(St.Anne's),she has got to go to Scotland and take the Math Olympiad competition so she could have a source of funding for entering St.Anne's.The problem is,Jess doesn't have a car to take her family to Scotland. But in unexpected twist of fate,Mr. Ed Nicholls,a rich cleaning client of her and a computer wizard,offered her to drive them to Scotland just to escape his own big trouble for a while.And this is where their weird,hilarious and adventurous story had began..<br /><br />This story is an inspiring,touching,uplifting family drama where you would be charmed by the features of the characters.My next favorite to Jess was Ed because inspite of his imperfection,lacks manner and attitude,or wasn't the best person in the world,I did admire him because he completely grew during the trip.And though he doesn't have children of his own,I loved the way he treated Nicky and Tanzie.And of course,I especially loved the moment when he helped Nicky with the kids who constantly bullied him.<br /><br />The story is more about honesty,kindness,understanding relationships,humanity,family,and most of all,this serves as an eye-opener to everyone who thinks they are poor,when in fact they are rich..I'm sure you do know what I mean,'cause having read this book deeply affected me that I had a lot of crying moments..(glad that I've read this in my room,or else my mum-in-law would think that my husband and I had a fight,hehe)<br /><br />This is my first of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes" title="Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Jojo Moyes</a>,and after reading this author's beautiful writing,I want to <b>READ ALL<b></b> of her books! Many thanks to my sister <b>AJ<b></b> for recommending me this book,and please do check her beautiful review as well on this one.(though I haven't read it yet,hehe..but now that I've read this,I'd do just right that!)^^</b></b></span>

<div id="review_766945747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/766945747" />
    <a title="Jeanne " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16160718-jeanne"><img alt="Jeanne " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410740995p2/16160718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/766945747?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanne " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanne " href="/user/show/16160718-jeanne">Jeanne </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19547751-one-plus-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16160718-jeanne?shelf=br">br</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer766945747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17688098362961896538"><b> ***** 5 YOLO stars *****</b><br/><br/>This is only my second book by Jojo Moyes, and she managed again to pull on all of my heartstrings. I adored the characters in this book, including the big slobbery dog. The book is told through 4 different perspectives,<br/><br/><b>Jess</b>- Single mom trying to raise her ten year old daughter and teen stepson while working two low paying jobs to make ends meet.<br/><br/><b>Ed</b> High tech business man who has recently landed himself in self induced legal hot water.<br/><br/><b>Tanzie</b> Ten year old math prodigy.<br/><br/><b>Nick</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17688098362961896538" style="display:none"><b> ***** 5 YOLO stars *****</b><br /><br />This is only my second book by Jojo Moyes, and she managed again to pull on all of my heartstrings. I adored the characters in this book, including the big slobbery dog. The book is told through 4 different perspectives,<br /><br /><b>Jess</b>- Single mom trying to raise her ten year old daughter and teen stepson while working two low paying jobs to make ends meet.<br /><br /><b>Ed</b> High tech business man who has recently landed himself in self induced legal hot water.<br /><br /><b>Tanzie</b> Ten year old math prodigy.<br /><br /><b>Nicky</b> Withdrawn teen stepson who is constantly being bullied.<br /><br />I don't like to give the story away, so I'll let you read the book to find out how these four quirky characters plus a dog end up going on a road trip to Scotland together. I was surprised by how much the events happening during this road trip made me laugh, and getting Ed's perspective on spending time with this family was priceless.<br /><br />I loved all of the characters, but I could especially relate to Jess. There is kind of a universal understanding when you are a mom, that it's your job to be positive and make everything seem OK, even when it's not. It can actually be a lot of pressure to be the one who is never allowed to have a meltdown. My favorite thing about the road trip was seeing Ed, who started out being a little snobbish, end up feeling humbled by this mom who holds things together with a positive attitude, even though the world never seems to give her a break.<br /><br />This book was extremely well written women's fiction/ chick lit. Even though a sweet romance develops, the focus is more on family, and persevering through difficult times. I would always recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>, but at the same time I think this book would be a great place to start for anyone new to this author. While this book was sweet and emotionally moving, it wasn't a sob fest:)<br /><br />* Thanks for another fun br Ami!! xo</span>
  <a data-text-id="17688098362961896538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5800583436202456657">One Plus One, Jojo Moyes<br/>One single mom. One chaotic family. One quirky stranger. One irresistible love story from author of Me Before You. Suppose your life sucks. A lot.   <span id="freeText5800583436202456657" style="display:none">One Plus One, Jojo Moyes<br />One single mom. One chaotic family. One quirky stranger. One irresistible love story from author of Me Before You. Suppose your life sucks. A lot. Your husband has done a vanishing act, your teenage stepson is being bullied and your math whiz daughter has a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity that you can’t afford to pay for. That’s Jess’s life in a nutshell—until an unexpected knight-in-shining-armor offers to rescue them. Only Jess’s knight turns out to be Geeky Ed, the obnoxious tech millionaire whose vacation home she happens to clean. But Ed has big problems of his own, and driving the dysfunctional family to the Math Olympiad feels like his first unselfish act in ages... maybe ever. Suppose your life sucks. A lot. Your husband has done a vanishing act, your teenage stepson is being bullied and your math whiz daughter has a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity that you can’t afford to pay for. That’s Jess’s life in a nutshell—until an unexpected knight-in-shining-armor offers to rescue them. Only Jess’s knight turns out to be Geeky Ed, the obnoxious tech millionaire whose vacation home she happens to clean. But Ed has big problems of his own, and driving the dysfunctional family to the Math Olympiad feels like his first unselfish act in ages... maybe ever. <br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز چهارم ماه تا نوزدهم 1397؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سده ی 21 م<br />عنوان: یک بعلاوه یک؛ نویسنده: جوجو مویز؛ مترجم: مرتضی حسنوند؛ تهران: آسو‏‫، 1396؛ در 656 ص؛ شابک: 9786008755098؛<br />عنوان: یک بعلاوه یک؛ نویسنده: جوجو مویز؛ مترجم: فاطمه سرباز؛ تهران: متن دیگر‏‫، 1396؛ در 561 ص؛ شابک: 9786008699385؛‬<br />عنوان: یک به‌علاوه یک؛ مولف: جوجو مویز ؛ مترجم: سیمین تاجدینی؛ ویراستار: سمیرا فتحعلی‌آشتیانی؛ تهران: انتشارات آتیسا‏‫، 1396؛ در 656 ص؛ شابک: 9786008399742؛‬<br />عنوان: یک بعلاوه یک؛ نویسنده: جوجو مویز ؛ مترجم: ناهید محمدی؛اصفهان : نگین ایران ‏‫، 1397؛ در 517 ص؛ شابک: 9786006230658؛‬<br />عنوان: یک بعلاوه یک؛ نویسنده: جوجو مویز ؛ مترجم: فاطمه امینی؛ تهران: شاپیگان کتاب ، ‏‫‏‏‏1398؛ در 471 ص؛ شابک: 9786008937036؛<br /><br />گاهی عرصه چنان بر انسان تنگ می‌شود که او ناچار به تصمیم‌ گیری عجیبی در زندگی‌ می‌شود. اگر انسان با علم به اشتباه خود تصمیم نادرستی بگیرد ذهن او مدام به دنبال یک توجیه درست و منطقی برای این تصمیم می‌گردد. در نهایت زمانی که عواقب اشتباه خود را می‌بیند تمام سعی خود را می‌کند تا اشتباهاتش را جبران کند. اما چه کسی می‌تواند بدون کمک و همراهی دیگران به تنهایی از پس همه‌ ی مشکلات بر بیاید. همیشه گفته‌ اند یک دست صدا ندارد. «جوجو مویز» هم در رمان حیرت‌ انگیز «یک به علاوه یک» از همراهی عشق و دوستی برای جبران اشتباهات می‌گوید. رمان بلند و عاشقانه‌ ی «یک به علاوه یک» در 40 بخش به صورت دانای کل روایت می‌شود. یک به علاوه یک داستان زندگی مادری 27 ساله ی تنها و بی‌ پشتوانه به نام «جسیکا توماس» است، که به سختی در دو نوبت کار می‌کند، تا از پس هزینه‌ های زندگی خانواده‌ اش بر بیاید. همسرش «مارتی» دو سال پیش «جس» را با دختر و پسرش ترک کرده است. «جس» تمام سعی خود را می‌کند، تا با درآمد ناچيز به عنوان نظافت‌چی خانه‌ ای در دریا کنار، و کار در کافه، روی پای خود بایستد، و بتواند از«تانزی» دخترش حمایت کند، و از پسر همسرش «نیکی»، که با آن‌ها زندگی می‌کند، و رفتارهای عجیبی دارد مراقبت کند. «جس» همیشه لبخند می‌زند، و باور دارد، که همه چیز به نتیجه خواهد رسید. اما زمانی که او متوجه می‌شود، دخترش «تانزی» برای مسابقات ریاضی، باید به شهر دیگری برود، و آن‌ها به پول نیاز دارند، شرایط سخت‌تر می‌شود. او با مشکلات مالی دست و پنجه نرم می‌کند، و بازهم تمام تلاش خود را می‌کند، تا به عقب حرکت نکند. اما چیزهایی در زندگی است که به تنهایی حل نمی‌شوند، و هیچ‌کس در زندگی به «جس» یاد نداده است، که درخواست از دیگران اشکالی ندارد. داستان با آشنایی «جسیکا» و «اد نیکلاس»، رنگ‌ و بوی دیگری می‌گیرد، و همه چیز عوض می‌شود. نیکلاس مرد موفق و ثروتمندی است، که به دلیل ارتکاب یک اشتباه بزرگ در گذشته، پشیمان است، و تصمیم گرفته تا اشتباهاتش را جبران کند. او مدتی را برای استراحت، و فکر کردن به دریاکنار آمده است، و حالا کارفرمای «جسیکا»ست، که طی ماجرایی تصمیم به همراهی «جسیکا» می‌گیرد. آن‌ها یک سفر جاده‌ ای را آغاز می‌کنند، تا «تانزی» را به مسابقات، و موفقیت درسیش نزدیک کنند. اما آیا «جسیکا» و «اد نیکلاس» می‌توانند در این سفر کنار هم بعلاوه شوند و به هم کمک کنند؟ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer781868828865754788">I absolutely loved this book. I'd give it 10 stars if I could! JoJo Moyes' book, "Me Before You", is one of my favorite novels. I read a couple of her other books and didn't like them. I didn't expect much from this book just assuming "Me Before You" was a fluke. Boy was I wrong! It's a lighter read then "Me Before You" but it is wonderful in its own right. This was such a great story with wonderful characters. I laughed and I cried and I didn't want to put it down. </span>

<div id="review_976277593" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/976277593" />
    <a title="Jenna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24806763-jenna"><img alt="Jenna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396102867p2/24806763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/976277593?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna " href="/user/show/24806763-jenna">Jenna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525426585" href="/book/show/18693716-one-plus-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24806763-jenna?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24806763-jenna?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24806763-jenna?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24806763-jenna?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer976277593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11760783587066614210"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I am such a fan of “Me Before You” that I naturally started this book with pretty high expectations. So the question is, ‘Did this book live up to my expectations?’ I have struggled with this question not only while I was reading but for some time after I finished this book.<br/><br/>Up until around the 15% mark of this book, I kind of had trouble following the story. It seemed to jump around to different character’s POV before I could grasp an understanding of what was going on. This became a bi</span>
  <span id="freeText11760783587066614210" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />I am such a fan of “Me Before You” that I naturally started this book with pretty high expectations. So the question is, ‘Did this book live up to my expectations?’ I have struggled with this question not only while I was reading but for some time after I finished this book.<br /><br />Up until around the 15% mark of this book, I kind of had trouble following the story. It seemed to jump around to different character’s POV before I could grasp an understanding of what was going on. This became a bit distracting for me. But once I did, I was definitely hooked.<br /><br />I feel that once I was pulled into the story that the author did a fantastic job of building up the characters and making them come to life. Once I finished the book, I felt a bit nostalgic and disappointed that this quirky family was no longer going to be a part of my life. (One of those silly nuances of being a book nerd!) I honestly felt close to them all. So that answers part of the ‘yes’ in the initial question if this book could live up to the prior one that I read.<br /><br />I struggled a bit during certain aspects of the story and these moments pulled me out of the story and I found that to be a disappointment at times. For instance, one of the main characters (Jess) teaches her children proper morals and how honesty is important in life, yet she vandalizes another woman’s property (because of a man) out of anger but never seems to apologize to the woman for her actions or the damage that she caused and I didin’t feel that went along with her character that was so well established up until that point in the story. I also couldn’t help but think if this story were true that it isn’t something that people just ignore but there are usually financial consequences and angry people when these instances happen so it drew out of the story a bit.<br /><br />I also struggled with the ensuing drunken mishap that later took place between the two main characters (Jess and Ed). It just seems to me that if a drunk woman were to do the things that she did to and around a man whom she had only really gotten to know in the span of a couple of days, any man would have bolted straight out of there. So, it was confusing that he calmed her when she acted insane and yet was upset by something that happened later in the book that wasn’t quite as crazy, but more desperate. It just didn’t blend very well for me during this part of the book for me. I also found Ed’s sisters reaction to their breakup to be unbelievable. <br /><br />Those were my biggest hangups an dthey were minor compared to the rest of the book. There always seemed to be some action going on in the plot which I loved because I not once became bored. I was totally hooked into the story and was always curious of what would happen next and I love books that pull this interest from me.<br /><br />I have become a true fan on Jojo Moyes and I very much look forward to her next one! I think that this is a fun read and I highly recommend it to those out there who love a quirky love story. This is a perfect summer read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11760783587066614210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
